<th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sanskrit_language" title="Sanskrit language">Sanskrit</a></th>
<td><span lang="san">गौतम बुद्ध</span></td>

</table>
<p><b>Gautama Buddha</b> (c. 563 BCE/480 BCE – c. 483 BCE/400 BCE), also known as <b>Siddhārtha Gautama</b>, <b>Shakyamuni Buddha</b>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[note 3]</a></sup> or simply the <b>Buddha</b>, after the title of <i><a href="/wiki/Buddha_(title)" title="Buddha (title)">Buddha</a></i>, was an ascetic (<a href="/wiki/%C5%9Arama%E1%B9%87a" title="Śramaṇa">śramaṇa</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Sage_(philosophy)" title="Sage (philosophy)">sage</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBaroni2002230_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaroni2002230-6">[3]</a></sup> on whose teachings <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> was founded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[web 2]</a></sup> He is believed to have lived and taught mostly in the eastern part of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_India" title="Ancient India">ancient India</a> sometime between the sixth and fourth centuries <a href="/wiki/Common_Era" title="Common Era">BCE</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWarder200045_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWarder200045-9">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dating_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-dating-10">[note 4]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gautama taught a <a href="/wiki/Middle_Way" title="Middle Way">Middle Way</a> between sensual indulgence and the severe <a href="/wiki/Asceticism" title="Asceticism">asceticism</a> found in the <a href="/wiki/%C5%9Arama%E1%B9%87a" title="Śramaṇa">śramaṇa</a> movement<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELaumakis20084_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaumakis20084-11">[5]</a></sup> common in his region. He later taught throughout other regions of eastern India such as <a href="/wiki/Magadha" title="Magadha">Magadha</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kosala" title="Kosala">Kosala</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWarder200045_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWarder200045-9">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESkilton200441_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESkilton200441-12">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gautama is the primary figure in Buddhism. He is recognized by Buddhists as an <a href="/wiki/Enlightenment_in_Buddhism" title="Enlightenment in Buddhism">enlightened</a> or divine<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[7]</a></sup> teacher who attained full <a href="/wiki/Buddhahood" title="Buddhahood">Buddhahood</a>, and shared his insights to help <a href="/wiki/Sentient_beings_(Buddhism)" title="Sentient beings (Buddhism)">sentient beings</a> end rebirth and <a href="/wiki/Dukkha" title="Dukkha">suffering</a>. Accounts of his life, discourses, and <a href="/wiki/Monasticism" title="Monasticism">monastic</a> rules are believed by Buddhists to have been summarized after his death and memorized by his followers. Various collections of teachings attributed to him were passed down by <a href="/wiki/Oral_tradition" title="Oral tradition">oral tradition</a> and <a href="/wiki/P%C4%81li_Canon" title="Pāli Canon">first committed to writing</a> about 400 years later.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_Siddh.C4.81rtha_Gautama">Historical Siddhārtha Gautama</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mahajanapadas_(c._500_BCE).png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="889" data-file-width="1200" height="185" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Mahajanapadas_%28c._500_BCE%29.png/250px-Mahajanapadas_%28c._500_BCE%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Mahajanapadas_%28c._500_BCE%29.png/375px-Mahajanapadas_%28c._500_BCE%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Mahajanapadas_%28c._500_BCE%29.png/500px-Mahajanapadas_%28c._500_BCE%29.png 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mahajanapadas_(c._500_BCE).png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ancient kingdoms and cities of India during the time of the Buddha.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Scholars are hesitant to make unqualified claims about the historical facts of the Buddha's life. Most accept that he lived, taught and founded a monastic order during the <a href="/wiki/Mahajanapada" title="Mahajanapada">Mahajanapada</a> era during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Bimbisara" title="Bimbisara">Bimbisara</a> (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 558</span> – c.<span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 491 BCE</span>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[9]</a></sup> the ruler of the <a href="/wiki/Magadha" title="Magadha">Magadha</a> empire, and died during the early years of the reign of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ajatasatru" title="Ajatasatru">Ajasattu</a>, who was the successor of Bimbisara, thus making him a younger contemporary of <a href="/wiki/Mahavira" title="Mahavira">Mahavira</a>, the Jain <a href="/wiki/Tirthankara" title="Tirthankara">tirthankara</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith192434.2C_48_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith192434.2C_48-16">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchumann20031-5_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchumann20031-5-17">[11]</a></sup> Apart from the <a href="/wiki/Vedas" title="Vedas">Vedic</a> <a href="/wiki/Brahmin" title="Brahmin">Brahmins</a>, the Buddha's lifetime coincided with the flourishing of influential <a href="/wiki/%C5%9Arama%E1%B9%87a" title="Śramaṇa">Śramaṇa schools</a> of thought like <a href="/wiki/%C4%80j%C4%ABvika" title="Ājīvika">Ājīvika</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charvaka" title="Charvaka">Cārvāka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jainism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Aj%C3%B1ana" title="Ajñana">Ajñana</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJayatilleke1963chpt._1-3_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJayatilleke1963chpt._1-3-18">[12]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brahmajala_Sutta" title="Brahmajala Sutta">Brahmajala Sutta</a> records sixty-two such schools of thought. It was also the age of influential thinkers like <a href="/wiki/Mahavira" title="Mahavira">Mahavira (referred to as 'Nigantha Nataputta' in Pali Canon)</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[13]</a></sup><a href="/wiki/Mahavira" title="Mahavira">)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Purana_Kassapa" title="Purana Kassapa">Pūraṇa Kassapa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Makkhali_Gosala" title="Makkhali Gosala">Makkhali Gosāla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ajita_Kesakambali" title="Ajita Kesakambali">Ajita Kesakambalī</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pakudha_Kaccayana" title="Pakudha Kaccayana">Pakudha Kaccāyana</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sanjaya_Belatthaputta" title="Sanjaya Belatthaputta">Sañjaya Belaṭṭhaputta</a>, as recorded in <a href="/wiki/Sama%C3%B1%C3%B1aphala_Sutta" title="Samaññaphala Sutta">Samaññaphala Sutta</a>, whose viewpoints the Buddha most certainly must have been acquainted with.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWalshe1995268_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWalshe1995268-20">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollins2009199.E2.80.93200_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollins2009199.E2.80.93200-21">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[note 5]</a></sup> Indeed, <a href="/wiki/Sariputta" title="Sariputta">Sariputta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maudgalyayana" title="Maudgalyayana">Moggallāna</a>, two of the foremost disciples of the Buddha, were formerly the foremost disciples of Sañjaya Belaṭṭhaputta, the skeptic;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENakamura198020_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENakamura198020-24">[16]</a></sup> and the Pali canon frequently depicts Buddha engaging in debate with the adherents of rival schools of thoughts. Thus, Buddha was just one of the many śramaṇa philosophers of that time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWarder199845_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWarder199845-25">[17]</a></sup> There is also evidence to suggest that the two masters, <a href="/wiki/Alara_Kalama" title="Alara Kalama">Alara Kalama</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uddaka_Ramaputta" title="Uddaka Ramaputta">Uddaka Ramaputta</a>, were indeed historical figures and they most probably taught Buddha two different forms of meditative techniques.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWynne20078.E2.80.9323ch._2_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWynne20078.E2.80.9323ch._2-26">[18]</a></sup> While the general sequence of "birth, maturity, renunciation, search, awakening and liberation, teaching, death" is widely accepted,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarrithers2001_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarrithers2001-27">[19]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (December 2015)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup> there is less consensus on the veracity of many details contained in traditional biographies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBuswell2003352_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBuswell2003352-28">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELopez199516_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELopez199516-29">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>The times of Gautama's birth and death are uncertain. Most historians in the early 20th century dated his lifetime as circa 563 BCE to 483 BCE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECousins199657.E2.80.9363_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECousins199657.E2.80.9363-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchumann200310.E2.80.9313_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchumann200310.E2.80.9313-30">[22]</a></sup> More recently his death is dated later, between 411 and 400 BCE, while at a symposium on this question held in 1988,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBechert1991-1997_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBechert1991-1997-31">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERuegg199982-87_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERuegg199982-87-32">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENarain1993187-201_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENarain1993187-201-33">[25]</a></sup> the majority of those who presented definite opinions gave dates within 20 years either side of 400 BCE for the Buddha's death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECousins199657.E2.80.9363_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECousins199657.E2.80.9363-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrebish20082_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrebish20082-34">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dating_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-dating-10">[note 4]</a></sup> These alternative chronologies, however, have not yet been accepted by all historians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchumann2003xv_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchumann2003xv-39">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWayman199337.E2.80.9358_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWayman199337.E2.80.9358-40">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[note 6]</a></sup></p>
<p>The evidence of the early texts suggests that Siddhārtha Gautama was born into the <a href="/wiki/Shakya" title="Shakya">Shakya</a> clan, a community that was on the periphery, both geographically and culturally, of the eastern Indian subcontinent in the 5th century BCE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGombrich198849_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGombrich198849-46">[34]</a></sup> It was either a small republic, or an <a href="/wiki/Oligarchy" title="Oligarchy">oligarchy</a>, and his father was an elected chieftain, or oligarch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGombrich198849_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGombrich198849-46">[34]</a></sup> According to the Buddhist tradition, Gautama was born in <a href="/wiki/Lumbini" title="Lumbini">Lumbini</a>, now in modern-day <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a>, and raised in the Shakya capital of Kapilvastu, which may have been either in what is present day <a href="/wiki/Tilaurakot" title="Tilaurakot">Tilaurakot</a>, Nepal or <a href="/wiki/Piprahwa" title="Piprahwa">Piprahwa</a>, India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-birthplace_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-birthplace-3">[note 1]</a></sup> He obtained his enlightenment in <a href="/wiki/Bodh_Gaya" title="Bodh Gaya">Bodh Gaya</a>, gave his first sermon in <a href="/wiki/Sarnath" title="Sarnath">Sarnath</a>, and died in <a href="/wiki/Kushinagar" title="Kushinagar">Kushinagar</a>.</p>
<p>No written records about Gautama were found from his lifetime or some centuries thereafter. One <a href="/wiki/Edicts_of_Ashoka" title="Edicts of Ashoka">Edict of Asoka</a>, who reigned from circa 269 BCE to 232 BCE, commemorates the Emperor's pilgrimage to the Buddha's birthplace in <a href="/wiki/Lumbini" title="Lumbini">Lumbini</a>. Another one of his edicts mentions the titles of several <i><a href="/wiki/Dharma" title="Dharma">Dhamma</a></i> texts, establishing the existence of a written Buddhist tradition at least by the time of the <a href="/wiki/Maurya_Empire" title="Maurya Empire">Maurya era</a>. These texts may be the precursor of the <a href="/wiki/P%C4%81li_Canon" title="Pāli Canon">Pāli Canon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDhammika1993_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDhammika1993-64">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[web 10]</a></sup> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[note 7]</a></sup> The oldest surviving Buddhist manuscripts are the <a href="/wiki/Gandh%C4%81ran_Buddhist_texts" title="Gandhāran Buddhist texts">Gandhāran Buddhist texts</a>, reported to have been found in or around <a href="/wiki/Hadda,_Afghanistan" title="Hadda, Afghanistan">Haḍḍa</a> near <a href="/wiki/Jalalabad" title="Jalalabad">Jalalabad</a> in eastern <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> and now preserved in the <a href="/wiki/British_Library" title="British Library">British Library</a>. They are written in the <a href="/wiki/G%C4%81ndh%C4%81r%C4%AB_language" title="Gāndhārī language">Gāndhārī language</a> using the <a href="/wiki/Kharosthi" title="Kharosthi">Kharosthi</a> script on twenty-seven <a href="/wiki/Birch_bark_manuscript" title="Birch bark manuscript">birch bark manuscripts</a> and date from the first century BCE to the third century CE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[web 11]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditional_biographies">Traditional biographies</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Buddha-painting.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2894" data-file-width="2099" height="303" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Buddha-painting.jpg/220px-Buddha-painting.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Buddha-painting.jpg/330px-Buddha-painting.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Buddha-painting.jpg/440px-Buddha-painting.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Buddha-painting.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Buddha by <a href="/wiki/Otgonbayar_Ershuu" title="Otgonbayar Ershuu">Otgonbayar Ershuu</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biographical_sources">Biographical sources</span></h3>
<p>The sources for the life of Siddhārtha Gautama are a variety of different, and sometimes conflicting, traditional biographies. These include the <i><a href="/wiki/Buddhacarita" title="Buddhacarita">Buddhacarita</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Lalitavistara_S%C5%ABtra" title="Lalitavistara Sūtra">Lalitavistara Sūtra</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Mah%C4%81vastu" title="Mahāvastu">Mahāvastu</a></i>, and the <i>Nidānakathā</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFowler200532_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFowler200532-68">[49]</a></sup> Of these, the <i>Buddhacarita</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeal1883_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeal1883-69">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECowell1894_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECowell1894-70">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWillemen2009_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWillemen2009-71">[52]</a></sup> is the earliest full biography, an epic poem written by the poet <a href="/wiki/A%C5%9Bvagho%E1%B9%A3a" title="Aśvaghoṣa">Aśvaghoṣa</a> in the first century CE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[53]</a></sup> The <i>Lalitavistara Sūtra</i> is the next oldest biography, a <a href="/wiki/Mahayana" title="Mahayana">Mahāyāna</a>/<a href="/wiki/Sarvastivada" title="Sarvastivada">Sarvāstivāda</a> biography dating to the 3rd century CE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKaretzky2000xxi_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKaretzky2000xxi-73">[54]</a></sup> The <i>Mahāvastu</i> from the <a href="/wiki/Mah%C4%81s%C4%81%E1%B9%83ghika" title="Mahāsāṃghika">Mahāsāṃghika</a> <a href="/wiki/Lokottarav%C4%81da" title="Lokottaravāda">Lokottaravāda</a> tradition is another major biography, composed incrementally until perhaps the 4th century CE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKaretzky2000xxi_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKaretzky2000xxi-73">[54]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Dharmaguptaka" title="Dharmaguptaka">Dharmaguptaka</a> biography of the Buddha is the most exhaustive, and is entitled the <i>Abhiniṣkramaṇa Sūtra</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeal1875_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeal1875-74">[55]</a></sup> and various Chinese translations of this date between the 3rd and 6th century CE. The <i>Nidānakathā</i> is from the <a href="/wiki/Theravada" title="Theravada">Theravada</a> tradition in <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> and was composed in the 5th century by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhaghosa" title="Buddhaghosa">Buddhaghoṣa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESwearer2004177_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESwearer2004177-75">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>From canonical sources, the <a href="/wiki/Jataka_tales" title="Jataka tales">Jataka tales</a>, the <i>Mahapadana Sutta</i> (DN 14), and the <i>Achariyabhuta Sutta</i> (MN 123) which include selective accounts that may be older, but are not full biographies. The Jātakas retell previous lives of Gautama as a <a href="/wiki/Bodhisattva" title="Bodhisattva">bodhisattva</a>, and the first collection of these can be dated among the earliest Buddhist texts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchober200220_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchober200220-76">[57]</a></sup> The <i>Mahāpadāna Sutta</i> and <i>Achariyabhuta Sutta</i> both recount miraculous events surrounding Gautama's birth, such as the bodhisattva's descent from the <a href="/wiki/Tushita" title="Tushita">Tuṣita Heaven</a> into his mother's womb.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nature_of_traditional_depictions">Nature of traditional depictions</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Astasahasrika_Prajnaparamita_Queen_Maya_Birth.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="271" data-file-width="453" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Astasahasrika_Prajnaparamita_Queen_Maya_Birth.jpeg/220px-Astasahasrika_Prajnaparamita_Queen_Maya_Birth.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Astasahasrika_Prajnaparamita_Queen_Maya_Birth.jpeg/330px-Astasahasrika_Prajnaparamita_Queen_Maya_Birth.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Astasahasrika_Prajnaparamita_Queen_Maya_Birth.jpeg/440px-Astasahasrika_Prajnaparamita_Queen_Maya_Birth.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Astasahasrika_Prajnaparamita_Queen_Maya_Birth.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Maya_(mother_of_the_Buddha)" title="Maya (mother of the Buddha)">Māyā</a> miraculously giving birth to Siddhārtha. <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palm-leaf_manuscript" title="Palm-leaf manuscript">palm-leaf manuscript</a>. <a href="/wiki/Nalanda" title="Nalanda">Nālandā</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bihar" title="Bihar">Bihar</a>, India. <a href="/wiki/Pala_Empire" title="Pala Empire">Pāla period</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the earliest Buddhists texts, the <a href="/wiki/Nik%C4%81ya" title="Nikāya">nikāyas</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C4%80gama_(Buddhism)" title="Āgama (Buddhism)">āgamas</a>, the Buddha is not depicted as possessing <a href="/wiki/Omniscience" title="Omniscience">omniscience</a> (<i>sabbaññu</i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-77">[58]</a></sup> nor is he depicted as being an eternal transcendent (<i>lokottara</i>) being. According to <a href="/wiki/Bhikkhu_Analayo" title="Bhikkhu Analayo">Bhikkhu Analayo</a>, ideas of the Buddha's omniscience (along with an increasing tendency to deify him and his biography) are found only later, in the <a href="/wiki/Mahayana_sutras" title="Mahayana sutras">Mahayana sutras</a> and later <a href="/wiki/Pali" title="Pali">Pali</a> commentaries or texts such as the <i>Mahāvastu</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-77">[58]</a></sup> In the <i>Sandaka Sutta</i>, the Buddha's disciple Ananda outlines an argument against the claims of teachers who say they are all knowing <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[web 12]</a></sup> while in the <i>Tevijjavacchagotta Sutta</i> the Buddha himself states that he has never made a claim to being omniscient, instead he claimed to have the "higher knowledges" (<a href="/wiki/Abhij%C3%B1%C4%81" title="Abhijñā">abhijñā</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[59]</a></sup> The earliest biographical material from the Pali Nikayas focuses on the Buddha's life as a <a href="/wiki/%C5%9Arama%E1%B9%87a" title="Śramaṇa">śramaṇa</a>, his search for enlightenment under various teachers such as <a href="/wiki/Alara_Kalama" title="Alara Kalama">Alara Kalama</a> and his forty five year career as a teacher.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[web 13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Traditional biographies of Gautama generally include numerous miracles, omens, and supernatural events. The character of the Buddha in these traditional biographies is often that of a fully transcendent (Skt. <i>lokottara</i>) and perfected being who is unencumbered by the mundane world. In the <i>Mahāvastu</i>, over the course of many lives, Gautama is said to have developed supra-mundane abilities including: a painless birth conceived without intercourse; no need for sleep, food, medicine, or bathing, although engaging in such "in conformity with the world"; omniscience, and the ability to "suppress karma".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJones1956_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJones1956-81">[60]</a></sup> Nevertheless, some of the more ordinary details of his life have been gathered from these traditional sources. In modern times there has been an attempt to form a <a href="/wiki/Secularity" title="Secularity">secular understanding</a> of Siddhārtha Gautama's life by omitting the traditional supernatural elements of his early biographies.</p>
<p>Andrew Skilton writes that the Buddha was never historically regarded by Buddhist traditions as being merely human:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>It is important to stress that, despite modern Theravada teachings to the contrary (often a sop to skeptical Western pupils), he was never seen as being merely human. For instance, he is often described as having the thirty-two major and eighty minor marks or signs of a <i>mahāpuruṣa</i>, "superman"; the Buddha himself denied that he was either a man or a <a href="/wiki/Deva_(Buddhism)" title="Deva (Buddhism)">god</a>; and in the <i><a href="/wiki/Mahaparinibbana_Sutta" title="Mahaparinibbana Sutta">Mahāparinibbāna Sutta</a></i> he states that he could live for an <a href="/wiki/Kalpa_(aeon)" title="Kalpa (aeon)">aeon</a> were he asked to do so.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESkilton200464-65_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESkilton200464-65-82">[61]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>The ancient Indians were generally unconcerned with chronologies, being more focused on philosophy. Buddhist texts reflect this tendency, providing a clearer picture of what Gautama may have taught than of the dates of the events in his life. These texts contain descriptions of the culture and daily life of ancient India which can be corroborated from the <a href="/wiki/Jain_Agamas" title="Jain Agamas">Jain scriptures</a>, and make the Buddha's time the earliest period in <a href="/wiki/History_of_India" title="History of India">Indian history</a> for which significant accounts exist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarrithers200115_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarrithers200115-83">[62]</a></sup> British author <a href="/wiki/Karen_Armstrong" title="Karen Armstrong">Karen Armstrong</a> writes that although there is very little information that can be considered historically sound, we can be reasonably confident that Siddhārtha Gautama did exist as a historical figure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmstrong2000xii_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmstrong2000xii-84">[63]</a></sup> Michael Carrithers goes a bit further by stating that the most general outline of "birth, maturity, renunciation, search, awakening and liberation, teaching, death" must be true.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarrithers2001_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarrithers2001-27">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Biography">Biography</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conception_and_birth">Conception and birth</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maya_dream_of_the_Birth_of_Gautama_Siddharta.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1776" data-file-width="2548" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Maya_dream_of_the_Birth_of_Gautama_Siddharta.jpg/220px-Maya_dream_of_the_Birth_of_Gautama_Siddharta.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Maya_dream_of_the_Birth_of_Gautama_Siddharta.jpg/330px-Maya_dream_of_the_Birth_of_Gautama_Siddharta.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Maya_dream_of_the_Birth_of_Gautama_Siddharta.jpg/440px-Maya_dream_of_the_Birth_of_Gautama_Siddharta.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Maya_dream_of_the_Birth_of_Gautama_Siddharta.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Maya's dream of the Birth of Gautama Siddharta</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Birthplacebuddha.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1552" data-file-width="1552" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Birthplacebuddha.jpg/220px-Birthplacebuddha.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Birthplacebuddha.jpg/330px-Birthplacebuddha.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Birthplacebuddha.jpg/440px-Birthplacebuddha.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Birthplacebuddha.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Purported birthplace of Gautama Buddha in <a href="/wiki/Lumbini" title="Lumbini">Lumbini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-birthplace_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-birthplace-3">[note 1]</a></sup> a holy shrine also for many non-Buddhists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-google260_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-google260-85">[note 8]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Buddhist tradition regards <a href="/wiki/Lumbini" title="Lumbini">Lumbini</a>, in present-day <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a> to be the birthplace of the Buddha.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeise2013_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeise2013-86">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-birthplace_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-birthplace-3">[note 1]</a></sup> He grew up in <a href="/wiki/Kapilavastu" title="Kapilavastu">Kapilavastu</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-birthplace_3-4"><a href="#cite_note-birthplace-3">[note 1]</a></sup> The exact site of ancient Kapilavastu is unknown.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETrainor2010436-437_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETrainor2010436-437-87">[65]</a></sup> It may have been either <a href="/wiki/Piprahwa" title="Piprahwa">Piprahwa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh" title="Uttar Pradesh">Uttar Pradesh</a>, present-day India,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENakamura198018_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENakamura198018-59">[43]</a></sup> or <a href="/wiki/Tilaurakot" title="Tilaurakot">Tilaurakot</a>, present-day <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuntington1988_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuntington1988-88">[66]</a></sup> Both places belonged to the Sakya territory, and are located only 15 miles apart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuntington1988_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuntington1988-88">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gautama was born as a <a href="/wiki/Kshatriya" title="Kshatriya">Kshatriya</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESamuel2010_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESamuel2010-89">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[note 9]</a></sup> the son of <a href="/wiki/%C5%9Auddhodana" title="Śuddhodana">Śuddhodana</a>, "an elected chief of the <a href="/wiki/Shakya" title="Shakya">Shakya clan</a>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWarder200045_9-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWarder200045-9">[4]</a></sup> whose capital was Kapilavastu, and who were later annexed by the growing Kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Kosala" title="Kosala">Kosala</a> during the Buddha's lifetime. Gautama was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Family_name" title="Family name">family name</a>. His mother, <a href="/wiki/Maya_(mother_of_the_Buddha)" title="Maya (mother of the Buddha)">Maya</a> (Māyādevī), Suddhodana's wife, was a <a href="/wiki/Koli_people" title="Koli people">Koliyan</a> princess. Legend has it that, on the night Siddhartha was conceived, Queen Maya dreamt that a <a href="/wiki/White_elephant_(animal)" title="White elephant (animal)">white elephant</a> with six white tusks entered her right side,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeal187537_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeal187537-92">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJones195211_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJones195211-93">[70]</a></sup> and ten <a href="/wiki/Lunar_month" title="Lunar month">months</a> later<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeal187541_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeal187541-94">[71]</a></sup> Siddhartha was born. As was the Shakya tradition, when his mother Queen Maya became pregnant, she left Kapilvastu for her father's kingdom to give birth. However, her son is said to have been born on the way, at Lumbini, in a garden beneath a <a href="/wiki/Shorea_robusta" title="Shorea robusta">sal tree</a>.</p>
<p>The day of the Buddha's birth is widely celebrated in Theravada countries as <a href="/wiki/Vesak" title="Vesak">Vesak</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETurpie20013_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETurpie20013-95">[72]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Buddha%27s_Birthday" title="Buddha's Birthday">Buddha's Birthday</a> is called <i>Buddha <a href="/wiki/Purnima" title="Purnima">Purnima</a></i> in Nepal, Bangladesh, and India as he is believed to have been born on a full moon day. Various sources hold that the Buddha's mother died at his birth, a few days or seven days later. The infant was given the name Siddhartha (Pāli: Siddhattha), meaning "he who achieves his aim". During the birth celebrations, the hermit seer <a href="/wiki/Asita" title="Asita">Asita</a> journeyed from his mountain abode and announced that the child would either become a great king (<a href="/wiki/Chakravartin" title="Chakravartin">chakravartin</a>) or a great <a href="/wiki/Sadhu" title="Sadhu">sadhu</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENarada19929.E2.80.9312_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENarada19929.E2.80.9312-96">[73]</a></sup> By traditional account,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too vague attribution or weasel words. (November 2010)">which?</span></a></i>]</sup> this occurred after Siddhartha placed his feet in Asita's hair and Asita examined the birthmarks. Suddhodana held a naming ceremony on the fifth day, and invited eight <a href="/wiki/Brahmin" title="Brahmin">Brahmin</a> scholars to read the future. All gave a dual prediction that the baby would either become a great king or a great holy man.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENarada19929.E2.80.9312_96-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENarada19929.E2.80.9312-96">[73]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kaundinya" title="Kaundinya">Kondañña</a>, the youngest, and later to be the first <a href="/wiki/Arhat" title="Arhat">arhat</a> other than the Buddha, was reputed to be the only one who unequivocally predicted that Siddhartha would become a <a href="/wiki/Buddhahood" title="Buddhahood">Buddha</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENarada199211-12_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENarada199211-12-97">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>While later tradition and legend characterized Śuddhodana as a <a href="/wiki/Hereditary_monarchy" title="Hereditary monarchy">hereditary monarch</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kinship" title="Kinship">descendant</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Suryavansha" title="Suryavansha">Suryavansha</a> (Solar dynasty) of <span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="International Alphabet of Sanskrit Transliteration">Ikṣvāku</span> (Pāli: Okkāka), many scholars think that Śuddhodana was the elected chief of a tribal confederacy.</p>
<p>Early texts suggest that Gautama was not familiar with the dominant religious teachings of his time until he left on his religious quest, which is said to have been motivated by existential concern for the human condition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHamilton200047_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHamilton200047-98">[75]</a></sup> The state of the Shakya clan was not a monarchy, and seems to have been structured either as an <a href="/wiki/Oligarchy" title="Oligarchy">oligarchy</a>, or as a form of republic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGombrich198849-50_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGombrich198849-50-99">[76]</a></sup> The more egalitarian gana-sangha form of government, as a political alternative to the strongly hierarchical kingdoms, may have influenced the development of the śramanic <a href="/wiki/Jain_monasticism" title="Jain monasticism">Jain</a> and Buddhist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sangha_(Buddhism)" title="Sangha (Buddhism)">sanghas</a>, where monarchies tended toward <a href="/wiki/Historical_Vedic_religion" title="Historical Vedic religion">Vedic Brahmanism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThapar2002146_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThapar2002146-100">[77]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life_and_marriage">Early life and marriage</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Departure_of_Siddhartha.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2970" data-file-width="2022" height="250" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Departure_of_Siddhartha.jpg/170px-Departure_of_Siddhartha.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Departure_of_Siddhartha.jpg/255px-Departure_of_Siddhartha.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Departure_of_Siddhartha.jpg/340px-Departure_of_Siddhartha.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Departure_of_Siddhartha.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Departure of Prince Siddhartha</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Siddhartha was brought up by his mother's younger sister, <a href="/wiki/Mahapajapati_Gotami" title="Mahapajapati Gotami">Maha Pajapati</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENarada199214_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENarada199214-101">[78]</a></sup> By tradition, he is said to have been destined by birth to the life of a prince, and had three palaces (for seasonal occupation) built for him. Although more recent scholarship doubts this status, his father, said to be King Śuddhodana, wishing for his son to be a great king, is said to have shielded him from religious teachings and from knowledge of human <a href="/wiki/Dukkha" title="Dukkha">suffering</a>.</p>
<p>When he reached the age of 16, his father reputedly arranged his marriage to a cousin of the same age named <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yashodhara" title="Yashodhara">Yaśodharā</a> (Pāli: Yasodharā). According to the traditional account,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too vague attribution or weasel words. (November 2010)">which?</span></a></i>]</sup> she gave birth to a son, named <a href="/wiki/R%C4%81hula" title="Rāhula">Rāhula</a>. Siddhartha is said to have spent 29 years as a prince in <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Kapilavastu_(Shakya_capital)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Kapilavastu (Shakya capital) (page does not exist)">Kapilavastu</a>. Although his father ensured that Siddhartha was provided with everything he could want or need, Buddhist scriptures say that the future Buddha felt that material wealth was not life's ultimate goal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENarada199214_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENarada199214-101">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Renunciation_and_ascetic_life">Renunciation and ascetic life</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Victory_of_Buddha.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2913" data-file-width="2032" height="315" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/The_Victory_of_Buddha.jpg/220px-The_Victory_of_Buddha.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/The_Victory_of_Buddha.jpg/330px-The_Victory_of_Buddha.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/The_Victory_of_Buddha.jpg/440px-The_Victory_of_Buddha.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Victory_of_Buddha.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Victory of Buddha</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Great_Departure.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1095" data-file-width="4154" height="58" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Great_Departure.JPG/220px-Great_Departure.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Great_Departure.JPG/330px-Great_Departure.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Great_Departure.JPG/440px-Great_Departure.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Great_Departure.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The "Great Departure" of Siddhartha Gautama, surrounded by a <a href="/wiki/Halo_(religious_iconography)" title="Halo (religious iconography)">halo</a>, he is accompanied by numerous guards, <a href="/wiki/Maithuna" title="Maithuna">maithuna</a> loving couples, and <a href="/wiki/Devata" title="Devata">devata</a> who have come to pay homage; <a href="/wiki/Gandhara" title="Gandhara">Gandhara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kushan_Empire" title="Kushan Empire">Kushan period</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Siddharta_Gautama_Borobudur.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1440" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Siddharta_Gautama_Borobudur.jpg/220px-Siddharta_Gautama_Borobudur.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Siddharta_Gautama_Borobudur.jpg/330px-Siddharta_Gautama_Borobudur.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Siddharta_Gautama_Borobudur.jpg/440px-Siddharta_Gautama_Borobudur.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Siddharta_Gautama_Borobudur.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Prince Siddhartha shaves his hair and becomes an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ascetic" title="Ascetic">ascetic</a>. <a href="/wiki/Borobudur" title="Borobudur">Borobudur</a>, 8th century</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the age of 29 Siddhartha left his palace to meet his subjects. Despite his father's efforts to hide from him the sick, aged and suffering, Siddhartha was said to have seen an old man. When his charioteer <a href="/wiki/Channa_(Buddhist)" title="Channa (Buddhist)">Channa</a> explained to him that all people grew old, the prince went on further trips beyond the palace. On these he encountered a <a href="/wiki/Disease" title="Disease">diseased</a> man, a decaying <a href="/wiki/Cadaver" title="Cadaver">corpse</a>, and an <a href="/wiki/Asceticism" title="Asceticism">ascetic</a>. These depressed him, and he initially strove to overcome aging, sickness, and death by living the life of an ascetic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEConze195939-40_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEConze195939-40-102">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>Accompanied by Channa and riding his horse <a href="/wiki/Kanthaka" title="Kanthaka">Kanthaka</a>, Gautama quit his palace for the life of a <a href="/wiki/Mendicant" title="Mendicant">mendicant</a>. It's said that, "the horse's hooves were muffled by the gods"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENarada199215-16_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENarada199215-16-103">[80]</a></sup> to prevent guards from knowing of his departure.</p>
<p>Gautama initially went to <a href="/wiki/Rajgir" title="Rajgir">Rajagaha</a> and began his ascetic life by begging for alms in the street. After King Bimbisara's men recognised Siddhartha and the king learned of his quest, Bimbisara offered Siddhartha the throne. Siddhartha rejected the offer, but promised to visit his kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Magadha" title="Magadha">Magadha</a> first, upon attaining enlightenment.</p>
<p>He left Rajagaha and practised under two hermit teachers of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yogic" title="Yogic">yogic</a> meditation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUpadhyaya197195_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUpadhyaya197195-104">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELaumakis20088_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaumakis20088-105">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrubin2010_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrubin2010-106">[83]</a></sup> After mastering the teachings of <a href="/wiki/Alara_Kalama" title="Alara Kalama">Alara Kalama</a> (Skr. Ārāḍa Kālāma), he was asked by Kalama to succeed him. However, Gautama felt unsatisfied by the practice, and moved on to become a student of <a href="/wiki/Yoga" title="Yoga">yoga</a> with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Udaka_Ramaputta" title="Udaka Ramaputta">Udaka Ramaputta</a> (Skr. Udraka Rāmaputra).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmstrong200477_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmstrong200477-107">[84]</a></sup> With him he achieved high levels of meditative consciousness, and was again asked to succeed his teacher. But, once more, he was not satisfied, and again moved on.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENarada199219-20_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENarada199219-20-108">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>Siddhartha and a group of five companions led by <a href="/wiki/Kaundinya" title="Kaundinya">Kaundinya</a> are then said to have set out to take their austerities even further. They tried to find enlightenment through deprivation of worldly goods, including food, practising <a href="/wiki/Mortification_of_the_flesh" title="Mortification of the flesh">self-mortification</a>. After nearly starving himself to death by restricting his food intake to around a leaf or nut per day, he collapsed in a river while bathing and almost drowned. A village girl named Sujata gave him some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Payasam" title="Payasam">payasam</a> (a pudding made from milk and <a href="/wiki/Jaggery" title="Jaggery">jaggery</a>) after which Siddhartha got back some energy. Siddhartha began to reconsider his path. Then, he remembered a moment in childhood in which he had been watching his father start the season's ploughing. He attained a concentrated and focused state that was blissful and refreshing, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jh%C4%81na" title="Jhāna">jhāna</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Awakening">Awakening</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Astasahasrika_Prajnaparamita_Victory_Over_Mara.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="279" data-file-width="456" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Astasahasrika_Prajnaparamita_Victory_Over_Mara.jpeg/220px-Astasahasrika_Prajnaparamita_Victory_Over_Mara.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Astasahasrika_Prajnaparamita_Victory_Over_Mara.jpeg/330px-Astasahasrika_Prajnaparamita_Victory_Over_Mara.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Astasahasrika_Prajnaparamita_Victory_Over_Mara.jpeg/440px-Astasahasrika_Prajnaparamita_Victory_Over_Mara.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Astasahasrika_Prajnaparamita_Victory_Over_Mara.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Buddha surrounded by the demons of <a href="/wiki/Mara_(demon)" title="Mara (demon)">Māra</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palm_leaf_manuscript" title="Palm leaf manuscript">palm leaf manuscript</a>. <a href="/wiki/Nalanda" title="Nalanda">Nālandā</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bihar" title="Bihar">Bihar</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>. <a href="/wiki/Pala_Empire" title="Pala Empire">Pāla period</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Enlightenment_in_Buddhism" title="Enlightenment in Buddhism">Enlightenment in Buddhism</a></div>
<p>According to the early Buddhist texts,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sn56_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-sn56-109">[web 14]</a></sup> after realizing that meditative <a href="/wiki/Dhy%C4%81na_in_Buddhism" title="Dhyāna in Buddhism">dhyana</a> was the right path to awakening, but that extreme asceticism didn't work, Gautama discovered what Buddhists call the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Way" title="Middle Way">Middle Way</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sn56_109-1"><a href="#cite_note-sn56-109">[web 14]</a></sup>—a path of moderation away from the extremes of <a href="/wiki/Hedonism" title="Hedonism">self-indulgence</a> and self-mortification, or the <a href="/wiki/Noble_Eightfold_Path" title="Noble Eightfold Path">Noble Eightfold Path</a>, as described in the <a href="/wiki/Dhammacakkappavattana_Sutta" title="Dhammacakkappavattana Sutta">Dhammacakkappavattana Sutta</a>, which is regarded as the first discourse of the Buddha.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sn56_109-2"><a href="#cite_note-sn56-109">[web 14]</a></sup> In a famous incident, after becoming starved and weakened, he is said to have accepted milk and <a href="/wiki/Rice_pudding" title="Rice pudding">rice pudding</a> from a village girl named Sujata.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-goldenbowl_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-goldenbowl-110">[web 15]</a></sup> Such was his emaciated appearance that she wrongly believed him to be a spirit that had granted her a wish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-goldenbowl_110-1"><a href="#cite_note-goldenbowl-110">[web 15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following this incident, Gautama was famously seated under a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sacred_fig" title="Sacred fig">pipal</a> tree—now known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bodhi_tree" title="Bodhi tree">Bodhi tree</a>—in <a href="/wiki/Bodh_Gaya" title="Bodh Gaya">Bodh Gaya</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, when he vowed never to arise until he had found the truth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGyatso20078.E2.80.939_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGyatso20078.E2.80.939-111">[86]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kaundinya" title="Kaundinya">Kaundinya</a> and four other companions, believing that he had abandoned his search and become undisciplined, left. After a reputed 49 days of meditation, at the age of 35, he is said to have attained <a href="/wiki/Bodhi" title="Bodhi">Enlightenment</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGyatso20078.E2.80.939_111-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGyatso20078.E2.80.939-111">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-basicteaching_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-basicteaching-112">[web 16]</a></sup> and became known as the <i>Buddha</i> or "Awakened One" ("Buddha" is also sometimes translated as "The Enlightened One").</p>
<p>According to some sutras of the Pali canon, at the time of his awakening he realized complete insight into the <a href="/wiki/Four_Noble_Truths" title="Four Noble Truths">Four Noble Truths</a>, thereby attaining <a href="/wiki/Moksha" title="Moksha">liberation</a> from <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Samsara" title="Samsara">samsara</a></i>, the endless cycle of rebirth, suffering and dying again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson1999_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson1999-113">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams200274-75_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams200274-75-114">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB-DL_Four_Truths_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-EB-DL_Four_Truths-115">[web 17]</a></sup> According to scholars, this story of the awakening and the stress on "liberating insight" is a later development in the Buddhist tradition, where the Buddha may have regarded the practice of <i><a href="/wiki/Dhy%C4%81na_in_Buddhism" title="Dhyāna in Buddhism">dhyana</a></i> as leading to <a href="/wiki/Nirvana" title="Nirvana">Nirvana</a> and <i>moksha</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVetter1988xxi-xxxvii_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVetter1988xxi-xxxvii-116">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBronkhorst199399-100.2C_102-111_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBronkhorst199399-100.2C_102-111-117">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson1999_113-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson1999-113">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[note 10]</a></sup></p>
<p>Nirvana is the extinguishing of the "fires" of desire, hatred, and ignorance, that keep the cycle of suffering and rebirth going.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[91]</a></sup> Nirvana is also regarded as the "end of the world", in that no personal identity or boundaries of the mind remain.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In such a state, a being is said to possess the <a href="/wiki/Buddhahood#Ten_characteristics_of_a_Buddha" title="Buddhahood">Ten Characteristics</a>, belonging to every Buddha.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>According to a story in the <i>Āyācana Sutta</i> (Samyutta Nikaya VI.1) — a scripture found in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/P%C4%81li" title="Pāli">Pāli</a> and other <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/canon" title="wiktionary:canon">canons</a> — immediately after his awakening, the Buddha debated whether or not he should teach the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dharma_(Buddhism)" title="Dharma (Buddhism)">Dharma</a></i> to others. He was concerned that humans were so overpowered by ignorance, greed and hatred that they could never recognise the path, which is subtle, deep and hard to grasp. However, in the story, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brahma_(Buddhism)#Brahm.C4.81_Sahampati" title="Brahma (Buddhism)">Brahmā Sahampati</a> convinced him, arguing that at least some will understand it. The Buddha relented, and agreed to teach.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Formation_of_the_sangha">Formation of the sangha</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sarnath1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="532" data-file-width="800" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Sarnath1.jpg/220px-Sarnath1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Sarnath1.jpg/330px-Sarnath1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Sarnath1.jpg/440px-Sarnath1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sarnath1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Dhamek_Stupa" title="Dhamek Stupa">Dhamek Stupa</a> in Sârnâth, India, site of the first teaching of the Buddha in which he taught the <a href="/wiki/Four_Noble_Truths" title="Four Noble Truths">Four Noble Truths</a> to his first five disciples</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After his awakening, the Buddha met <a href="/wiki/Trapusa_and_Bahalika" title="Trapusa and Bahalika">Taphussa and Bhallika</a> — two merchant brothers from the city of <a href="/wiki/Balkh" title="Balkh">Balkh</a> in what is currently Afghanistan — who became his first lay disciples. It is said that each was given hairs from his head, which are now claimed to be enshrined as <a href="/wiki/%C5%9Aar%C4%ABra" title="Śarīra">relics</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shwe_Dagon" title="Shwe Dagon">Shwe Dagon</a> Temple in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rangoon" title="Rangoon">Rangoon</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Burma" title="Burma">Burma</a>. The Buddha intended to visit <a href="/wiki/Asita" title="Asita">Asita</a>, and his former teachers, <a href="/wiki/Alara_Kalama" title="Alara Kalama">Alara Kalama</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Udaka_Ramaputta" title="Udaka Ramaputta">Udaka Ramaputta</a>, to explain his findings, but they had already died.</p>
<p>He then travelled to the <a href="/wiki/Sarnath" title="Sarnath">Deer Park</a> near <a href="/wiki/Varanasi" title="Varanasi">Varanasi</a> (Benares) in northern India, where he set in motion what Buddhists call the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dharmacakra" title="Dharmacakra">Wheel of Dharma</a> by delivering his first sermon to the five companions with whom he had sought enlightenment. Together with him, they formed the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sangha_(Buddhism)" title="Sangha (Buddhism)"><span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="International Alphabet of Sanskrit Transliteration">saṅgha</span></a>: the company of Buddhist monks.</p>
<p>All five become <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arahants" title="Arahants">arahants</a>, and within the first two months, with the conversion of <a href="/wiki/Yasa" title="Yasa">Yasa</a> and fifty four of his friends, the number of such arahants is said to have grown to 60. The conversion of three brothers named Kassapa followed, with their reputed 200, 300 and 500 disciples, respectively. This swelled the sangha to more than 1,000.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Travels_and_teaching">Travels and teaching</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TheBuddhaAndVajrapaniGandhara2ndCentury.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2677" data-file-width="1794" height="254" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/TheBuddhaAndVajrapaniGandhara2ndCentury.jpg/170px-TheBuddhaAndVajrapaniGandhara2ndCentury.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/TheBuddhaAndVajrapaniGandhara2ndCentury.jpg/255px-TheBuddhaAndVajrapaniGandhara2ndCentury.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/TheBuddhaAndVajrapaniGandhara2ndCentury.jpg/340px-TheBuddhaAndVajrapaniGandhara2ndCentury.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TheBuddhaAndVajrapaniGandhara2ndCentury.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Buddha with his protector <a href="/wiki/Vajrapani" title="Vajrapani">Vajrapani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gandhara" title="Gandhara">Gandhāra</a>, 2nd century CE, Ostasiatische Kunst Museum</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>For the remaining 45 years of his life, the Buddha is said to have traveled in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gangetic_Plain" title="Gangetic Plain">Gangetic Plain</a>, in what is now <a href="/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh" title="Uttar Pradesh">Uttar Pradesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bihar" title="Bihar">Bihar</a>, and southern <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a>, teaching a diverse range of people: from nobles to servants, murderers such as <a href="/wiki/Angulimala" title="Angulimala">Angulimala</a>, and cannibals such as Alavaka.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMalalasekera1960291-292_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMalalasekera1960291-292-120">[92]</a></sup> Although the Buddha's language remains unknown, it's likely that he taught in one or more of a variety of closely related Middle Indo-Aryan dialects, of which <a href="/wiki/Pali" title="Pali">Pali</a> may be a standardization.</p>
<p>The sangha traveled through the subcontinent, expounding the dharma. This continued throughout the year, except during the four months of the <a href="/wiki/Vassa" title="Vassa">Vassa</a> rainy season when ascetics of all religions rarely traveled. One reason was that it was more difficult to do so without causing harm to animal life. At this time of year, the sangha would retreat to monasteries, public parks or forests, where people would come to them.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vulturepeak1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Vulturepeak1.jpg/220px-Vulturepeak1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Vulturepeak1.jpg/330px-Vulturepeak1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Vulturepeak1.jpg/440px-Vulturepeak1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vulturepeak1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A view of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Griddhraj_Parvat" title="Griddhraj Parvat">Vulture Peak</a>, where the <a href="/wiki/Atanatiya_Sutta" title="Atanatiya Sutta">Atanatiya Sutta</a> was held</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first vassana was spent at <a href="/wiki/Varanasi" title="Varanasi">Varanasi</a> when the sangha was formed. After this, the Buddha kept a promise to travel to <a href="/wiki/Rajgir" title="Rajgir">Rajagaha</a>, capital of <a href="/wiki/Magadha" title="Magadha">Magadha</a>, to visit King <a href="/wiki/Bimbisara" title="Bimbisara">Bimbisara</a>. During this visit, <a href="/wiki/Sariputta" title="Sariputta">Sariputta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maudgalyayana" title="Maudgalyayana">Maudgalyayana</a> were converted by <a href="/wiki/Assaji" title="Assaji">Assaji</a>, one of the first five disciples, after which they were to become the Buddha's two foremost followers. The Buddha spent the next three seasons at Veluvana Bamboo Grove monastery in Rajagaha, capital of Magadha.</p>
<p>Upon hearing of his son's awakening, Suddhodana sent, over a period, ten delegations to ask him to return to Kapilavastu. On the first nine occasions, the delegates failed to deliver the message, and instead joined the sangha to become arahants. The tenth delegation, led by Kaludayi, a childhood friend of Gautama's (who also became an arahant), however, delivered the message.</p>
<p>Now two years after his awakening, the Buddha agreed to return, and made a two-month journey by foot to Kapilavastu, teaching the dharma as he went. At his return, the royal palace prepared a midday meal, but the sangha was making an alms round in Kapilavastu. Hearing this, Suddhodana approached his son, the Buddha, saying:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>"Ours is the warrior lineage of Mahamassata, and not a single warrior has gone seeking alms."</p>
</blockquote>
<p>The Buddha is said to have replied:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>"That is not the custom of your royal lineage. But it is the custom of my Buddha lineage. Several thousands of Buddhas have gone by seeking alms."</p>
</blockquote>
<p>Buddhist texts say that Suddhodana invited the sangha into the palace for the meal, followed by a dharma talk. After this he is said to have become a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sotapanna" title="Sotapanna">sotapanna</a>. During the visit, many members of the royal family joined the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sangha_(Buddhism)" title="Sangha (Buddhism)">sangha</a>. The Buddha's cousins <a href="/wiki/Ananda" title="Ananda">Ananda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anuruddha" title="Anuruddha">Anuruddha</a> became two of his five chief disciples. At the age of seven, his son <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rahula" title="Rahula">Rahula</a> also joined, and became one of his ten chief disciples. His half-brother <a href="/wiki/Nanda_(Buddhist)" title="Nanda (Buddhist)">Nanda</a> also joined and became an arahant.</p>
<p>Of the Buddha's disciples, Sariputta, <a href="/wiki/Maudgalyayana" title="Maudgalyayana">Maudgalyayana</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mahakasyapa" title="Mahakasyapa">Mahakasyapa</a>, Ananda and Anuruddha are believed to have been the five closest to him. His ten foremost disciples were reputedly completed by the quintet of <a href="/wiki/Upali" title="Upali">Upali</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subhoti" title="Subhoti">Subhoti</a>, Rahula, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mahakaccana" title="Mahakaccana">Mahakaccana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Punna" title="Punna">Punna</a>.</p>
<p>In the fifth vassana, the Buddha was staying at Mahavana near <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vesali" title="Vesali">Vesali</a> when he heard news of the impending death of his father. He is said to have gone to Suddhodana and taught the dharma, after which his father became an arahant.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_last_days_of_buddha_teachings.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="789" data-file-width="1214" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/The_last_days_of_buddha_teachings.jpg/220px-The_last_days_of_buddha_teachings.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/The_last_days_of_buddha_teachings.jpg/330px-The_last_days_of_buddha_teachings.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/The_last_days_of_buddha_teachings.jpg/440px-The_last_days_of_buddha_teachings.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_last_days_of_buddha_teachings.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The last days of buddha teachings</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The king's death and cremation was to inspire the creation of an order of nuns. Buddhist texts record that the Buddha was reluctant to ordain women. His foster mother <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maha_Pajapati" title="Maha Pajapati">Maha Pajapati</a>, for example, approached him, asking to join the sangha, but he refused. Maha Pajapati, however, was so intent on the path of awakening that she led a group of royal Sakyan and Koliyan ladies, which followed the sangha on a long journey to Rajagaha. In time, after Ananda championed their cause, the Buddha is said to have reconsidered and, five years after the formation of the sangha, agreed to the ordination of women as nuns. He reasoned that males and females had an equal capacity for awakening. But he gave women additional rules (<a href="/wiki/Vinaya" title="Vinaya">Vinaya</a>) to follow.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mahaparinirvana">Mahaparinirvana</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Astasahasrika_Prajnaparamita_Buddha_Parinirvana.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="292" data-file-width="456" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Astasahasrika_Prajnaparamita_Buddha_Parinirvana.jpeg/220px-Astasahasrika_Prajnaparamita_Buddha_Parinirvana.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Astasahasrika_Prajnaparamita_Buddha_Parinirvana.jpeg/330px-Astasahasrika_Prajnaparamita_Buddha_Parinirvana.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Astasahasrika_Prajnaparamita_Buddha_Parinirvana.jpeg/440px-Astasahasrika_Prajnaparamita_Buddha_Parinirvana.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Astasahasrika_Prajnaparamita_Buddha_Parinirvana.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Buddha's entry into <a href="/wiki/Parinirvana" title="Parinirvana">Parinirvana</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palm_leaf_manuscript" title="Palm leaf manuscript">palm leaf manuscript</a>. <a href="/wiki/Nalanda" title="Nalanda">Nālandā</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bihar" title="Bihar">Bihar</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>. <a href="/wiki/Pala_Empire" title="Pala Empire">Pāla period</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Buddha%27s_cremation_stupa,_Kushinagar.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Buddha%27s_cremation_stupa%2C_Kushinagar.jpg/220px-Buddha%27s_cremation_stupa%2C_Kushinagar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Buddha%27s_cremation_stupa%2C_Kushinagar.jpg/330px-Buddha%27s_cremation_stupa%2C_Kushinagar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Buddha%27s_cremation_stupa%2C_Kushinagar.jpg/440px-Buddha%27s_cremation_stupa%2C_Kushinagar.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Buddha%27s_cremation_stupa,_Kushinagar.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Buddha's cremation stupa, <a href="/wiki/Kushinagar" title="Kushinagar">Kushinagar</a> (Kushinara).</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EndAscetism.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="945" data-file-width="1586" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/EndAscetism.JPG/220px-EndAscetism.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/EndAscetism.JPG/330px-EndAscetism.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/EndAscetism.JPG/440px-EndAscetism.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EndAscetism.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The sharing of the <a href="/wiki/%C5%9Aar%C4%ABra" title="Śarīra">relics of the Buddha</a>, Zenyōmitsu-Temple Museum, Tokyo</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to the <i>Mahaparinibbana Sutta</i> of the Pali canon, at the age of 80, the Buddha announced that he would soon reach Parinirvana, or the final deathless state, and abandon his earthly body. After this, the Buddha ate his last meal, which he had received as an offering from a blacksmith named <a href="/wiki/Cunda_(Buddhism)" title="Cunda (Buddhism)">Cunda</a>. Falling violently ill, Buddha instructed his attendant <a href="/wiki/Ananda" title="Ananda">Ānanda</a> to convince Cunda that the meal eaten at his place had nothing to do with his passing and that his meal would be a source of the greatest merit as it provided the last meal for a Buddha.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[web 18]</a></sup> Mettanando and <a href="/wiki/Oskar_von_Hin%C3%BCber" title="Oskar von Hinüber">von Hinüber</a> argue that the Buddha died of <a href="/wiki/Superior_mesenteric_artery_syndrome" title="Superior mesenteric artery syndrome">mesenteric</a> <a href="/wiki/Infarction" title="Infarction">infarction</a>, a symptom of old age, rather than food poisoning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMettanando2000_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMettanando2000-122">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[web 19]</a></sup></p>
<p>The precise contents of the Buddha's final meal are not clear, due to variant scriptural traditions and ambiguity over the translation of certain significant terms; the <a href="/wiki/Theravada" title="Theravada">Theravada</a> tradition generally believes that the Buddha was offered some kind of pork, while the <a href="/wiki/Mahayana" title="Mahayana">Mahayana</a> tradition believes that the Buddha consumed some sort of truffle or other mushroom. These may reflect the different traditional views on <a href="/wiki/Buddhist_vegetarianism" title="Buddhist vegetarianism">Buddhist vegetarianism</a> and the precepts for monks and nuns.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Arthur_Waley" title="Arthur Waley">Waley</a> suggests that Theravadins would take <i>suukaramaddava</i> (the contents of the Buddha's last meal), which can translate literally as <i>pig-soft</i>, to mean "soft flesh of a pig" or "pig's soft-food", that is, after <a href="/wiki/Karl_Eugen_Neumann" title="Karl Eugen Neumann">Neumann</a>, a soft food favoured by pigs, assumed to be a <a href="/wiki/Truffle" title="Truffle">truffle</a>. He argues (also after Neumann) that as "(p)lant names tend to be local and dialectical", as there are several plants known to have <i>suukara-</i> (pig) as part of their names,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wayley1932_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wayley1932-124">[note 11]</a></sup> and as Pali Buddhism developed in an area remote from the Buddha's death, <i>suukaramaddava</i> could easily have been a type of plant whose local name was unknown to those in Pali regions. Specifically, local writers writing soon after the Buddha's death knew more about their flora than Theravadin commentator <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhaghosa" title="Buddhaghosa">Buddhaghosa</a> who lived hundreds of years and hundreds of kilometres remote in time and space from the events described. Unaware that it may have been a local plant name and with no Theravadin prohibition against eating animal flesh, Theravadins would not have questioned the Buddha eating meat and interpreted the term accordingly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWaley1932343.E2.80.9354_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWaley1932343.E2.80.9354-125">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to Buddhist tradition, the Buddha died at Kuśināra (present-day <a href="/wiki/Kushinagar" title="Kushinagar">Kushinagar</a>, India), which became a pilgrimage center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuntington198647_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuntington198647-126">[95]</a></sup> Ananda protested the Buddha's decision to enter Parinirvana in the abandoned jungles of <a href="/wiki/Kushinagar" title="Kushinagar">Kuśināra</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Malla_(India)" title="Malla (India)">Malla</a> kingdom. The Buddha, however, is said to have reminded Ananda how Kushinara was a land once ruled by a righteous wheel-turning king and the appropriate place for him to die.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVon_Hin.C3.BCber200949_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVon_Hin.C3.BCber200949-127">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Buddha then asked all the attendant <a href="/wiki/Bhikkhu" title="Bhikkhu">Bhikkhus</a> to clarify any doubts or questions they had and cleared them all in a way which others could not do. They had none. According to Buddhist scriptures, he then finally entered Parinirvana. The Buddha's final words are reported to have been: "All composite things (<a href="/wiki/Sa%E1%B9%85kh%C4%81ra" title="Saṅkhāra">Saṅkhāra</a>) are perishable. Strive for your own liberation with diligence" (Pali: 'vayadhammā saṅkhārā appamādena sampādethā'). His body was cremated and the <a href="/wiki/Relic" title="Relic">relics</a> were placed in monuments or stupas, some of which are believed to have survived until the present. For example, The <a href="/wiki/Temple_of_the_Tooth" title="Temple of the Tooth">Temple of the Tooth</a> or "Dalada Maligawa" in <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> is the place where what some believe to be the <a href="/wiki/Relic_of_the_tooth_of_the_Buddha" title="Relic of the tooth of the Buddha">relic of the right tooth of Buddha</a> is kept at present.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Life_Scenes_of_Buddha_-_Birth-Enlightenment-Descent_from_Heaven-First_Sermon-Passing_Away_-_Circa_2nd_Century_CE_-_Rajghat_-_ACCN_00-H-1_-_Government_Museum_-_Mathura_2013-02-23_5843.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Life_Scenes_of_Buddha_-_Birth-Enlightenment-Descent_from_Heaven-First_Sermon-Passing_Away_-_Circa_2nd_Century_CE_-_Rajghat_-_ACCN_00-H-1_-_Government_Museum_-_Mathura_2013-02-23_5843.JPG/220px-thumbnail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Life_Scenes_of_Buddha_-_Birth-Enlightenment-Descent_from_Heaven-First_Sermon-Passing_Away_-_Circa_2nd_Century_CE_-_Rajghat_-_ACCN_00-H-1_-_Government_Museum_-_Mathura_2013-02-23_5843.JPG/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Life_Scenes_of_Buddha_-_Birth-Enlightenment-Descent_from_Heaven-First_Sermon-Passing_Away_-_Circa_2nd_Century_CE_-_Rajghat_-_ACCN_00-H-1_-_Government_Museum_-_Mathura_2013-02-23_5843.JPG/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Life_Scenes_of_Buddha_-_Birth-Enlightenment-Descent_from_Heaven-First_Sermon-Passing_Away_-_Circa_2nd_Century_CE_-_Rajghat_-_ACCN_00-H-1_-_Government_Museum_-_Mathura_2013-02-23_5843.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Life scenes of Buddha, sand stone: Birth, Enlightenment, Descent from Heaven, First Sermon, Passing Away, c. 2nd Century CE, <a href="/wiki/Government_Museum,_Mathura" title="Government Museum, Mathura">Government Museum, Mathura</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to the Pāli historical chronicles of Sri Lanka, the <a href="/wiki/Dipavamsa" title="Dipavamsa"><span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="International Alphabet of Sanskrit Transliteration">Dīpavaṃsa</span></a> and <a href="/wiki/Mahavamsa" title="Mahavamsa"><span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="International Alphabet of Sanskrit Transliteration">Mahāvaṃsa</span></a>, the coronation of <a href="/wiki/Ashoka" title="Ashoka">Emperor Aśoka</a> (Pāli: Asoka) is 218 years after the death of the Buddha. According to two textual records in Chinese (<span lang="zh">十八部論</span> and <span lang="zh">部執異論</span>), the coronation of Emperor Aśoka is 116 years after the death of the Buddha. Therefore, the time of Buddha's passing is either 486 BCE according to Theravāda record or 383 BCE according to Mahayana record. However, the actual date traditionally accepted as the date of the Buddha's death in Theravāda countries is 544 or 545 BCE, because the reign of Emperor Aśoka was traditionally reckoned to be about 60 years earlier than current estimates. In Burmese Buddhist tradition, the date of the Buddha's death is 13 May 544 BCE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKala172439_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKala172439-128">[97]</a></sup> whereas in Thai tradition it is 11 March 545 BCE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEade199515.E2.80.9316_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEade199515.E2.80.9316-129">[98]</a></sup></p>
<p>At his death, the Buddha is famously believed to have told his disciples to follow no leader. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mahakasyapa" title="Mahakasyapa">Mahakasyapa</a> was chosen by the sangha to be the chairman of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_Buddhist_Council" title="First Buddhist Council">First Buddhist Council</a>, with the two chief disciples <a href="/wiki/Maudgalyayana" title="Maudgalyayana">Maudgalyayana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sariputta" title="Sariputta">Sariputta</a> having died before the Buddha.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lord_Buddha_-_Hair_Relics.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Lord_Buddha_-_Hair_Relics.JPG/220px-Lord_Buddha_-_Hair_Relics.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Lord_Buddha_-_Hair_Relics.JPG/330px-Lord_Buddha_-_Hair_Relics.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Lord_Buddha_-_Hair_Relics.JPG/440px-Lord_Buddha_-_Hair_Relics.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
